guide\n\n# The relationship between sketches and prompts\n\nVizcom creates a unique partnership between your sketch and your prompt:\n\n- Your sketch provides the foundational form, proportions, and layout\n\n- Your prompt fills in details, materials, finishes, and rendering style\n\n\nThis relationship is adjustable through the [influence percentage](https://www.vizcom.ai/). Higher influence gives more weight to your sketch's exact form, while lower influence allows your prompt to have more interpretation on the final result.\n\n**Understanding this relationship is crucial:** the same prompt applied to different sketches will yield different results, and different prompts applied to the same sketch will produce varied outcomes.\n\n**Example:**\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/PlCRWm6pYmWBhoLyAvTzDTQ.png)\n\n[â€¹ Prompts as design intent](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/prompts-as-design-intent)\n\n[Structure of effective prompts â€º](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/structure-of-effective-prompts)\n\n[iframe](https://edit.framer.com/?framerSiteId=3e326915499184beab1bba7824b41116cf2f9ee548da32018ec9519b55e29a9b&nodeId=fynNNibs0&source=www.vizcom.ai&features=%7B%22editorBarOnPageEditing%22%3Afalse%7D)", html=None, rawHtml=None, links=None, extract=None, json=None, screenshot=None, metadata={'ogDescription': 'Vizcom turns your sketches into stunning concept drawings in seconds. guide\n\n# Structure of effective prompts\n\n### Basic anatomy of an effective prompt:\n\n> Include key components such as `subject`, `style`, `materials`, `context`, and `technical parameters` to clearly communicate your design intent.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/Yrx58zYCYdcFXKVLKHxus7beCsY.png)\n\n### Here are some examples of these components:\n\n1. **Subject**: What you're designing\n\nExample: `office chair, sports car, coffee machine`\n\n2. **Style**: Design language or aesthetic direction\n\nExample: `minimalist, industrial, organic`\n\n3. **Materials & Finishes**: Physical properties. What materials should it appear to be made of?\n\nExample: `brushed aluminum, walnut veneer, matte plastic`\n\n4. **Context / Environment**: Setting or background: where is this object or element used or viewed?\n\nExample: `studio environment, outdoor scene, contextual setting`\n\n5. **Technical Parameters**: Rendering details and specifications\n\nExample: `photorealistic, isometric view, cutaway`\n\n\n> ðŸ’¡ While not every prompt needs all these elements, including relevant ones for your specific project will yield the best results.\n\n#### Example 1:\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/P5W1DsYEtAK5wpiKYxlpH7K7U.png)\n\n### Example 2:\n\nPrompt: `Vintage scrambler motorcycle, 70s aesthetic, metal tank, leather seat, knobby tires`\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/X6Bu23mqbpHgr6oJUohuASb856A.png)\n\n[â€¹ The relationship between sketches and prompts](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/the-relationship-between-sketches-and-prompts)\n\n[Ideal prompt lengths â€º](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/ideal-prompt-lengths)\n\n[iframe](https://edit.framer.com/?framerSiteId=3e326915499184beab1bba7824b41116cf2f9ee548da32018ec9519b55e29a9b&nodeId=luvtjb6oJ&source=www.vizcom.ai&features=%7B%22editorBarOnPageEditing%22%3Afalse%7D)", html=None, rawHtml=None, links=None, extract=None, json=None, screenshot=None, metadata={'og:description': 'Vizcom turns your sketches into stunning concept drawings in seconds. guide\n\n# What are prompts?\n\n### Definition: Text instructions that guide Vizcom's interpretation of your sketch\n\nIn Vizcom, a prompt is a set of text instructions that directs how the AI transforms your sketch. Unlike general AI image generators that create images from text alone, Vizcom's prompts work in conjunction with your sketch to create a refined visual output.\n\n> **A prompt might look like this:**\n\n`Modern office chair, ergonomic design, brushed aluminum frame, black mesh fabric, product photography, studio lighting, white background, photorealistic rendering`\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/wNsNYTBTJR8qgw7AFDGhR7TUwKU.jpg)\n\nThis tells Vizcom what you're designing `an office chair`, its style `modern, ergonomic`, materials `brushed aluminum frame, black mesh fabric`, and how it should be rendered `product photography, studio lighting, white background, photorealistic rendering`.\n\n\\\\_\\\\_\\\\_\n\n### Here is another example:\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/tq7pZUzzvhmpUgeN24KNE7I.png)\n\nThe image above was created with the prompt:\n\n`hyperrealistic:1.5), silver, modern, electric supercar, Car design concept, (depth of field:1.5), blurred background (dark studio scene:1.8), glowing light blue taillight, monochrome scene, glossy, reflective surfaces, colorful particles flying around, DSLR `\n\nNotice that this prompt loosely follows a structure: `**[subject], [prepositional details], [setting], [meta modifiers];**`\n\n**\\\\* Tip:** consider including a brand name in your design to help establish a strong and cohesive design language.\n\n[â€¹ Vizcom in your workflow](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/vizcom-in-your-workflow)\n\n[Prompts as design intent Drag in an Animate block and connect it to a generation or scene you want to bring to life. From there, all it takes is a prompt.\n\nPrompting for animation works a little differently than prompting for still images. Vizcom already understands your starting image, so instead of describing details about colors and textures, focus on how things\xa0_move_. What is the object doing? How should the camera react? Are there people entering the frame or interacting with your design.\n\n_Animation prompt: Boat, sleek white hull, sparkling blue ocean, sunlit sky, gentle waves lapping, boat rocking slightly. camera moving in waves_\n\n#### What kind of stories can you tell?\n\nDesigners are already using Animate to explore motion, context, and interaction early in the process, when ideas are still forming. Here are a few workflows and prompts you can try with your concepts.\n\n##### Turntable rotation\n\nShow every angle of your design by rotating it in place, like a product reveal or studio shot.\n\n_Animation prompt: Turntable rotation of chair design, 360 degree smooth motion orbit._\n\n##### Interaction in context\n\nAdd a hand reaching into frame to pick up a tool, or a user sitting in a chair, simple ways to ground your design in real use.\n\n_Animation prompt: Power drill, cordless design, metallic finish, robust grip, light reflections shifting. single hand entering the frame from the left gripping drill and pulling trigger, lifting drill up out of frame with smooth motion._\n\n_Sketch, render, environment reference, animate. Animate prompt: Pastel chunky sneaker design, person wearing shoe, white sock, person taking step forward out of frame, slight zoom out._\n\n_Animation prompt: People walking into frame and sitting in chairs_\n\n##### Facial expressions and body language\n\nFor concept art and character exploration, Animate helps visualize subtle emotion or posture shifts that bring a persona to life.\n\n_Animation Prompts from top left to bottom right: 1-Elf touching forehead, sighing deeply, frustrated but composed emotion. 2-Elf crossing arms, slight smirk, raised eyebrow, skeptical expression. 3-Elf raising hands to cheeks in surprised emotion. 4-Elf with angry facial expression screaming at person._\n\n##### Camera reveals\n\nSlowly pan across a scene to uncover details, focus attention, or add a cinematic layer to your concept presentation\n\n_Animation Prompt: Castle, perched on rocky cliffs, ancient stone walls, towering turrets, drone shot zoom out to show adventurer back standing on mountain looking at castle, camera focus shift to person, blurs out background, illustrative style_\n\n##### Apparel Try On\n\nAnimate a model trying on apparel, turning in frame, or walking through space to bring fashion and product visuals to life.\n\n_Sketch, render, remove background, try on, animate. Animate prompt: Guy turns around, puts on the hood of the jacket and walks away from the camera._\n\n#### Access & Availability\n\nSince Animate is still in beta, each plan includes a limited number of animation credits per month. This helps us ensure quality and performance as we continue to improve the feature. Weâ€™re actively working on ways to expand access and introduce options for purchasing additional credits soon.\n\nAnimation in the Enterprise plan includes enhanced privacy and security, which may introduce slight variations in behavior compared to other plans.\n\n#### Your ideas in motion\n\nWith Animate, you can now express your ideas in motion adding interaction, behavior, and emotion to your concepts in seconds. However, we also believe that it is important to use AI in a way that empowers designers. There is a very real fear that AI could replace us, but it is of our belief that AI is simply a tool FOR designers, to help us work quickly and more creatively.\n\nOne of our core values is to ensure that designers maintain authorship over the generated designs and feel ownership over the final designs. We believe that designers should have control over the design process and that AI should be used as a tool to support their creativity, rather than as a replacement for their skills.\n\nInstagram post on Vizcom\'s account page, detailing CEO Jordan Taylor\'s mission to responsibly and ethically use AI to empower real people.\n\n## The era of AI\n\nThe era of AI is ever evolving, with the "move fast break things" mentality. Here at Vizcom, we\'re committed to responsibly and ethically harness the power of AI with the public images, and ensuring permissions when using artist data. We also prioritize security and privacy when it comes to AI-generated designs.\n\nWe understand that designers may have concerns about the security and ownership of their designs, and we take these concerns seriously. We have implemented robust security measures to ensure that designs are protected and that designers have control over who can access them.\n\n"We hear a lot about the fear that AI will replace jobs, but that\'s not quite right. AI is here to make our jobs easier - any tedious, time-consuming parts of rendering that you want to use AI for, AI will be able to assist you. Thatâ€™s why we built Palettes: to empower designers to teach AI about their own work, reflecting their style and values, not someone elseâ€™s. Unlike other companies, we stand for personal AI, fully owned and controlled by the creative.\n\n## Together, we can create responsibly.\n\n## **1\\. Use Your Own Work**  Create Palettes only with designs, artwork, or assets you own or have full rights to use.\n\n## **2\\. Honor Attribution**  Get clear permission before using collaborative or licensed work for training.\n\n## **3\\. Preserve Authenticity**  Focus on developing your unique style and not replicating someone elseâ€™s.\n\n## Why It Matters\n\n- ## **Protect Creativity**: Innovation thrives in a culture that values originality.\n\n- ## **Respect Artists**: Give credit where itâ€™s due, and support fair practices.\n\n- ## **Build Trust**: Foster a creative community rooted in integrity and collaboration.\n\n- ## **Empower Designers**: Lead creative work with your own voice and vision.\n\n\n## Our Promise\n\n## Palettes is designed for creativity, not appropriation. guide\n\n# Common prompt mistakes\n\n## Overly vague descriptions\n\n> âš ï¸ _Vague prompts like_ `"nice chair"` _or "_ `modern product"` _provide too little guidance, forcing Vizcom to make too many assumptions about your intent. This often results in generic outputs that don\'t align with your vision._\n\n**Instead of:** `"sleek product"`\n\n**Try:** `"sleek wireless earbuds case, soft-touch matte plastic, contoured form"`\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/YKtMv6WYpku98VGobQ63BLI3Fg4.png)\n\n## Contradictory instructions\n\n> âš ï¸ _When prompts contain conflicting directives, Vizcom must reconcile these contradictions, often leading to unpredictable results._\n\n**Contradictory:** `"minimalist chair with ornate detailing and complex patterns"`\n\n**Clearer:** `"minimalist chair with subtle textured details on armrests"`\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/TqvxH4qhgWchZIhZ7peZob2ONoA.png)\n\n## Unrealistic expectations\n\n> âš ï¸ _Prompts that ask for physically impossible or contradictory material properties can confuse the AI._\n\n**Unrealistic:** `"completely transparent metal chair"`\n\n**More realistic:** `"chair with transparent acrylic legs and thin brushed metal frame"`\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/1HWxzfu7ddPPmFDpQ6Ku92WMj80.png)\n\n## Missing critical components\n\nOmitting key information forces Vizcom to make assumptions that might not align with your intent. Commonly forgotten elements include:\n\n- Main material specifications\n\n- Viewing angle or perspective\n\n- Rendering style (photorealistic vs. stylized)\n\n\nEven a simple addition like `"photorealistic rendering"` or `"matte plastic finish"` can significantly improve results.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/6uAL6CExLAw5UfCPHomD8DilU.png)\n\n[â€¹ Ideal prompt lengths](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/ideal-prompt-lengths)\n\n[When prompting is not enough â€º](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/when-prompting-is-not-enough)\n\n[iframe](https://edit.framer.com/?framerSiteId=3e326915499184beab1bba7824b41116cf2f9ee548da32018ec9519b55e29a9b&nodeId=Oq0kWbh72&source=www.vizcom.ai&features=%7B%22editorBarOnPageEditing%22%3Afalse%7D)', html=None, rawHtml=None, links=None, extract=None, json=None, screenshot=None, metadata={'description': 'Vizcom turns your sketches into stunning concept drawings in seconds. Crafting a good chair balances form, proportions, ergonomics, and manufacturing techniques. This challenge led team member Chris Ference to consider how Vizcomâ€™s rendering and 3D capabilities could enhance the design process and enable him to create a chair in just two days.\n\nThe exploration focused on creating rotomolded and injection molded chairs suitable for outdoor or dining settings. The process began with rough sketches, then transitioned into Vizcom to visualize ideas in higher fidelity. This approach allowed for the identification of strong concepts, the elimination of weaker ones, and continued ideation with greater intention and focus.\n\nThrough rounds of generating 3D forms, sketching over them, and generating new images, a deeper understanding of the desired chair design was achieved. Evaluating a number of 3D prints provided a new way to review and critique the work. The ability to hold the sketch in physical form was a unique aspect of the workflow that was found invaluable.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/XugPK3jucZtT9lu4qLKkb2Z0c.jpg)\n\nThroughout the process, the aim was to create designs with a clear relationship between all elements of the chair, including the front legs, seat, backrest, and back feet. While drawing the side view of a chair, it was challenging to understand how this perspective would relate to the front and connect with the legs. The seat was envisioned as seamlessly connecting to the back and curving into the legs. By generating a 3D version of the sketch, a clearer understanding of how to resolve the form was gained.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/WF39AkEXKSygUZrUMuUouXJ5yg.jpg)\n\nUsing the generated 3D object, consistent representations of the idea were achieved from various angles. Recently, Turkish car designer and YouTuber Berk Kaplan visited the Moholy-Nagy University of Art and Design (MOME) in Budapest to conduct a three-day digital sketching workshop for Vehicle Design specialization students. The workshop not only covered the fundamentals of digital sketching but also explored the growing relationship between AI and design, providing valuable insights into the future of automotive design and the importance of sketching in the era of AI.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/QW2o6Xk8TdRpA5jm1gdY8YiM5dA.jpg)\n\n#### The Importance of Sketching in Design Education\n\nSketching is a fundamental skill for designers across various disciplines, allowing them to visualize and communicate their ideas quickly. As Kaplan emphasized during the workshop, sketching helps to bridge the gap between the designer's mental image and the audience's understanding. By putting ideas on paper, designers can avoid misunderstandings and ensure everyone is on the same page. This is particularly crucial in the automotive industry, where clear visual communication is essential for successful collaboration between designers, engineers, and other stakeholders.\n\n#### AI and the Future of Creative Workflows\n\nIn addition to traditional sketching techniques, the workshop also focused on the integration of AI tools like Midjourney and Vizcom into the car design process. Kaplan highlighted the surprising ways in which AI can both complement and challenge the designer's vision. While tools like Midjourney can generate unexpected results based on text prompts, Vizcom supports the designer's creative process by directly enhancing their sketches. By leveraging AI technologies, designers can save time and explore new possibilities while still maintaining their unique artistic vision.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/4AcjMlEGm20dqpYOpw0lOTb8qQ8.jpg)\n\n#### The Impact on Design Education\n\nAs AI continues to shape the future of design, it is crucial for educational institutions like MOME to adapt their curricula and provide students with the skills and knowledge needed to thrive in this new landscape. By incorporating digital sketching and AI tools into their programs, universities can prepare the next generation of designers for the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead. However, it is equally important to emphasize the enduring value of traditional skills like sketching, which will continue to play a vital role in the design process, even as AI technologies become more prevalent.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/EYoRndPxnclctt4UiIig1PKIA.jpg)\n\nBerk Kaplan's digital sketching workshop at MOME highlights the importance of sketching in design education and the growing influence of AI on creative workflows. By embracing both traditional skills and emerging technologies, design students can position themselves for success in an increasingly complex and dynamic industry. His work, particularly with Vizcom, showcases a symbiotic relationship between human creativity and machine intelligence, transforming the way we think about design, collaboration, and innovation.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/vkXpNNtCgDM2ceR0t4KKRG110.jpg)\n\nAs we explore Mueller's philosophy and workflow, we see a journey that begins with a solitary idea and evolves through constant exchange into a fully fleshed-out product idea, ready to be refined and introduced to the world.\n\nBelow, Dennis shares his insights and experiences, offering a first-person perspective into how he's integrated AI tools like Vizcom into his creative processes.\n\n## What's a misconception about AI's role in design?\n\n_The Creative Co-Worker_\n\nPeople are always afraid of the New. IÂ´m always curious about it. So I started using AI design tools in 2021 and back then I thought it was kind of a nice gadget to play around with but did not see the whole potential behind it.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/cHa5zOuBtu6s0zSVZ8MKmOIAwU.jpg)\n\nFor sure AI in general is under discussion and that's an important thing to do now to compare the positive and negative effects it could cause. But to find out the potential, you need to try it and judge later on. I started using Vizcom heavily at the beginning of 2023. A thing I fell in love with was the intuitive user interface. Nothing distracts you, the functions are very clear and the settings are not overwhelming.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/sFvVJQZaZzxQcB3pOMwf79SRya0.jpg)\n\nI always begin with a hand-drawn sketch and a self-written prompt, laying the groundwork for my ideas in a traditional creative manner before digital rendering. Many misunderstand this part, but to me, it's akin to an early-stage collaborator where I share initial concepts shortly after starting a project. Effective communication, even in these nascent stages, is crucial for success. Engaging in clear, unbiased exchanges with tools like AI can significantly enhance the outcome.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/dGfMRfjqDVl6lYdPbWcE6E6GU.jpg)![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/SbOcnjWzlbhyvk1x7IcAHye2wug.jpg)\n\nIÂ´m not saying that you should always use AI tools but in some cases, it makes sense, especially when you're stuck with new ideas and have a kind of writer's block in design. Then I always use a sketch and put it into Vizcom to create new ideas or give the initial idea a twist, edge, and/or life.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/NoIjKc8OtUFvj9Pr55sy33nZUfQ.jpg)\n\nAnother misconception is that AI tools should just render out the idea you had in your mind. I use Vizcom very organically and go with the flow. But what does this mean? I never get stuck too much on that first idea.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/eLnvu7i3dCxxdSR9axmHJwZqKaE.jpg)\n\nI trust my instincts and stay alert for the intriguing. This approach requires a creative lens to spot and appreciate unique elements. Whenever something catches my eye, even a minor detail, I make a note of it to possibly blend with other designs, shapes, or materials later. I frequently employ Procreate for initial sketches, then transfer these ideas into Vizcom to add realism and depth.\n\nTry to see Vizcom as an extension of your creative mind rather than an enemy who's stealing your job. At the end, we still guide the whole journey and make the decisions.\n\n## How do you balance\xa0Vizcom\xa0with human-centric design?\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/XLNcJ33VfE5GkY9zgVmZr0qbhI.jpg)\n\nIn designing footwear, starting with the last is crucial, particularly for performance shoes, to ensure proper ergonomics and fit from the beginning. Typically, I begin with a side-view sketch as my foundation. From there, I refine my ideas by moving on to Vizcom. This stage helps me either polish my initial concept into a rendered version or explore new design directions.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/DmmDU4u7ivgmfG8edxDM4Uyc6s.jpg)![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/a5bVjEVmJNi1fE0jnX8pxv54s.png)\n\nA common misunderstanding about AI is thinking that once it generates hyper-realistic images, the work is complete. However, creating designs that truly cater to human needs involves multiple steps to ensure the final product is genuinely effective.\n\n## How do you see AI influencing the design process in the next 5 years?\n\nI told a lot of friends that it's an exciting time to be a designer. Sure we have some serious challenges\xa0to tackle but as soon as everybody understands the power of collaboration beautiful things can happen. Collaborations in all ways, people from different departments, companies, countries, and backgrounds, but also man and machines.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/dDRydkT3A86ByRhyeGHSscLyWk.jpg)\n\nIn the next 5 years, a lot of repetitive activities will be heavily influenced\xa0by AI in design. CMFs, Tech Packs, 3d to manufacture are just a few topics creatives won't spend as much time on as they used to. This is amazing because then we will have more resources to invest in storytelling, experimenting, questioning the status quo, finding real sustainable solutions, and interacting with people more often again.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/GMeBM4XciIEVHHKMfBtxUs81EVw.jpg)\n\nBesides the quantity and quality of creative ideas within a shorter timeframe\xa0will increase a lot. So, there needs to be good designers and core team members to judge all these results to take the right path.\n\n## Describe the most exciting aspect of merging industrial design with\xa0Vizcom.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/XiJCVF4WVtWiMXX5C5NwWW4ucks.jpg)![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/JphX3wEwQL95BYgy2tAAPlnlxkc.jpg)\n\nAs mentioned in the beginning, the real strength is having a coworker now all the time. Playing ping pong with ideas creates a unique energy\xa0where sometimes it doesn't\xa0feel like work. It's more like being in a flow state, comparable with a runner's high where one idea leads to the next.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/bnVkoQlTiuNuYdF9q2HfsYqqLI.jpg)\n\nIt can get you addicted in a way. It's that magical moment when Vizcom renders out a new vision in such a hyper-realistic way, that you feel that there is something special the world did not see before.\n\n## How can young designers & students best prepare for the AI-driven design landscape?\n\nI've always been a huge fan of building fundamentals\xa0in the beginning. Especially living in a digital world, we need to learn the basics like model making to understand our physical world first. This is a very important\xa0step a lot of creatives nowadays are missing.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/CNSdcLJxOafbAYIF1XwfzWNBVI.jpg)\n\nTo create innovative designs that stand the test of time, we must master ergonomics, refined silhouettes, seamless surface transitions, and the principles of the golden ratio, among other skills. It's crucial for young designers to begin incorporating these tools early in their careers. However, it's equally important for the emerging design culture to remain critical and challenge the status quo.\n\nðŸ‘‰ Learn more about Dennis Johann Mueller and his work [**here**](https://www.dennisjohannmueller.com/)\n\n[iframe](https://edit.framer.com/?framerSiteId=3e326915499184beab1bba7824b41116cf2f9ee548da32018ec9519b55e29a9b&nodeId=fF9eKZplp&source=www.vizcom.ai&features=%7B%22editorBarOnPageEditing%22%3Afalse%7D)", html=None, rawHtml=None, links=None, extract=None, json=None, screenshot=None, metadata={'og:url': 'https://www.vizcom.ai/blog/using-vizcom-as-a-co-creator-a-new-era-for-footwear-design', 'framer-search-index': 'https://framerusercontent.com/sites/1NDdwv2PBK7LOFnjSpkhqr/searchIndex-kT9PpIrwZP3c.json', 'og:type': 'website', 'twitter:title': 'AI as a Design Partner: A Conversation with Dennis Johann Mueller', 'description': 'As designers, we are storytellers. guide\n\n# Sketch with intent\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/VghAZck2co6cuGml6zWWX5CQvFo.png)\n\nAs design tools evolve, core principles remain essential. Understanding form, proportion, material properties, ergonomics, and manufacturing constraints becomes even more critical when working with AI assistance.\n\n**These fundamentals allow you to:**\n\n- Provide sketches that effectively communicate your intent\n\n- Evaluate AI outputs with a critical eye\n\n- Know when to accept AI suggestions and when to override them\n\n- Maintain design integrity throughout the process\n\n\nVizcom works best when guided by your design knowledge rather than when you expect AI to substitute for it.\n\n[â€¹ Vizcom as a tool](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/vizcom-as-a-tool)\n\n[Vizcom in your workflow â€º](https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/vizcom-in-your-workflow)\n\n[iframe](https://edit.framer.com/?framerSiteId=3e326915499184beab1bba7824b41116cf2f9ee548da32018ec9519b55e29a9b&nodeId=WtzSuwGdz&source=www.vizcom.ai&features=%7B%22editorBarOnPageEditing%22%3Afalse%7D)', html=None, rawHtml=None, links=None, extract=None, json=None, screenshot=None, metadata={'og:url': 'https://www.vizcom.ai/edu-prompting-guide/docs/sketch-with-intent', 'framer-search-index': 'https://framerusercontent.com/sites/1NDdwv2PBK7LOFnjSpkhqr/searchIndex-kT9PpIrwZP3c.json', 'og:description': 'Vizcom turns your sketches into stunning concept drawings in seconds. This significant milestone underscores our relentless commitment to implementing top-notch security measures that keep your data safe and secure.\n\n## What SOC 2 Type 1 Means for You\n\nService Organization Control (SOC) 2 Type 1 is an auditing procedure that ensures service providers like Vizcom securely manage your data to protect the interests of both the organization and the privacy of its clients. It focuses on non-financial reporting controls related to security, availability, processing integrity, confidentiality, and privacy of a system.\n\nIn practical terms, SOC 2 Type 1 compliance gives you, our client, the assurance that we have met the industryâ€™s high standard for security controls. This compliance serves as third-party validation of the design and implementation of our security processes, thus instilling a higher level of trust in our platform.\n\n## Our Journey to SOC 2 Type 1 Compliance\n\nAchieving SOC 2 Type 1 compliance has been a rigorous but highly rewarding journey. It involved the meticulous efforts of our DevOps, Security, and Compliance teams to align our practices with the high standards set by SOC 2 Type 1 requirements.\n\nFrom securing our cloud-based infrastructure on AWS, employing AES-256 encryption for data at rest and in transit, to implementing role-based access controls, every layer of our platform has been scrutinized and fortified.\n\n## Transparency and Trust\n\nWhile achieving SOC 2 Type 1 is an accomplishment we are proud of, it's not the final destination in our journey toward ensuring a secure and compliant platform. It serves as a baseline that informs and enhances our ongoing efforts to make Vizcom a safe environment for industrial designers from renowned enterprises such as Ford, Nike, and Toyota.\n\n## Conclusion\n\nWe would like to extend our deepest gratitude to our dedicated team and our loyal clients who trust us with their invaluable data. Our mission is to empower visionary minds, enabling them to bring their ideas to life with unprecedented efficiency and creativity. As part of our ongoing commitment to our users and their data, we are thrilled to announce that Vizcom has achieved SOC 2 Type II compliance.\n\n### What is SOC 2 Type II?\n\nSOC 2 (System and Organization Controls) Type II is a gold standard in data security. Developed by the American Institute of CPAs (AICPA), it evaluates an organizationâ€™s controls over time, ensuring they meet rigorous standards for security, availability, processing integrity, confidentiality, and privacy. Achieving this compliance demonstrates our unwavering dedication to protecting your data.\n\n### Why SOC 2 Type II Compliance Matters\n\nAt Vizcom, we understand that your design work is not just valuable; itâ€™s a part of your identity. Our Palette engine is built to develop your unique style, and itâ€™s essential that your data remains secure throughout this process. SOC 2 Type II compliance reassures you that your creative assets and personal information are handled with the highest level of security and care.\n\n### Our Journey to Compliance\n\nOur journey to SOC 2 Type II compliance was driven by our core values: authorship, personalization, security, and privacy. 10-30 words.** This provides enough detail to guide the AI without over-constraining it.\n\n#### Examples:\n\n**Too short (often vague):**\n\n`modern chair`\n\n**Effective length:**\n\n`ergonomic Crafting a good chair balances form, proportions, ergonomics, and manufacturing techniques. This challenge led team member Chris Ference to consider how Vizcomâ€™s rendering and 3D capabilities could enhance the design process and enable him to create a chair in just two days.\n\nThe exploration focused on creating rotomolded and injection molded chairs suitable for outdoor or dining settings. The process began with rough sketches, then transitioned into Vizcom to visualize ideas in higher fidelity. This approach allowed for the identification of strong concepts, the elimination of weaker ones, and continued ideation with greater intention and focus.\n\nThrough rounds of generating 3D forms, sketching over them, and generating new images, a deeper understanding of the desired chair design was achieved. Evaluating a number of 3D prints provided a new way to review and critique the work. The ability to hold the sketch in physical form was a unique aspect of the workflow that was found invaluable.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/XugPK3jucZtT9lu4qLKkb2Z0c.jpg)\n\nThroughout the process, the aim was to create designs with a clear relationship between all elements of the chair, including the front legs, seat, backrest, and back feet. While drawing the side view of a chair, it was challenging to understand how this perspective would relate to the front and connect with the legs. The seat was envisioned as seamlessly connecting to the back and curving into the legs. By generating a 3D version of the sketch, a clearer understanding of how to resolve the form was gained.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/WF39AkEXKSygUZrUMuUouXJ5yg.jpg)\n\nUsing the generated 3D object, consistent representations of the idea were achieved from various angles. Viewing the chair in its space through augmented reality also allowed for validation of proportions and seeing the chair at scale.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/OpOGfy6LWIAreM6FHzExNxwzOI.jpg)\n\nIn just 48 hours, Chris was able to ideate, refine, 3D print, and go through several iterations of the chair. With traditional tools, he might have been constrained by the extensive time required for visualization and development, limiting his ability to create multiple unique ideas. Sketching as a basis for image and 3D generation makes the ideation process feel seamless for designers. However, we also believe that it is important to use AI in a way that empowers designers. There is a very real fear that AI could replace us, but it is of our belief that AI is simply a tool FOR designers, to help us work quickly and more creatively.\n\nOne of our core values is to ensure that designers maintain authorship over the generated designs and feel ownership over the final designs. We believe that designers should have control over the design process and that AI should be used as a tool to support their creativity, rather than as a replacement for their skills.\n\nInstagram post on Vizcom\'s account page, detailing CEO Jordan Taylor\'s mission to responsibly and ethically use AI to empower real people.\n\n## The era of AI\n\nThe era of AI is ever evolving, with the "move fast break things" mentality. Here at Vizcom, we\'re committed to responsibly and ethically harness the power of AI with the public images, and ensuring permissions when using artist data. We also prioritize security and privacy when it comes to AI-generated designs.\n\nWe understand that designers may have concerns about the security and ownership of their designs, and we take these concerns seriously. We have implemented robust security measures to ensure that designs are protected and that designers have control over who can access them.\n\n"We hear a lot about the fear that AI will replace jobs, but that\'s not quite right. AI is here to make our jobs easier - any tedious, time-consuming parts of rendering that you want to use AI for, AI will be able to assist you. The real power in designers is our creativity and our personal taste - only real people, real designers can do that."\n\n## Conclusion\n\nFinally, we believe that it is important to listen to the design community, keep a finger on the pulse of the latest developments in AI, and make improvements to our design tool that meet our community\'s ever evolving needs. Drag in an Animate block and connect it to a generation or scene you want to bring to life. From there, all it takes is a prompt.\n\nPrompting for animation works a little differently than prompting for still images. Vizcom already understands your starting image, so instead of describing details about colors and textures, focus on how things\xa0_move_. What is the object doing? How should the camera react? Are there people entering the frame or interacting with your design.\n\n_Animation prompt: Boat, sleek white hull, sparkling blue ocean, sunlit sky, gentle waves lapping, boat rocking slightly. camera moving in waves_\n\n#### What kind of stories can you tell?\n\nDesigners are already using Animate to explore motion, context, and interaction early in the process, when ideas are still forming. Here are a few workflows and prompts you can try with your concepts.\n\n##### Turntable rotation\n\nShow every angle of your design by rotating it in place, like a product reveal or studio shot.\n\n_Animation prompt: Turntable rotation of chair design, 360 degree smooth motion orbit._\n\n##### Interaction in context\n\nAdd a hand reaching into frame to pick up a tool, or a user sitting in a chair, simple ways to ground your design in real use.\n\n_Animation prompt: Power drill, cordless design, metallic finish, robust grip, light reflections shifting. single hand entering the frame from the left gripping drill and pulling trigger, lifting drill up out of frame with smooth motion._\n\n_Sketch, render, environment reference, animate. Animate prompt: Pastel chunky sneaker design, person wearing shoe, white sock, person taking step forward out of frame, slight zoom out._\n\n_Animation prompt: People walking into frame and sitting in chairs_\n\n##### Facial expressions and body language\n\nFor concept art and character exploration, Animate helps visualize subtle emotion or posture shifts that bring a persona to life.\n\n_Animation Prompts from top left to bottom right: 1-Elf touching forehead, sighing deeply, frustrated but composed emotion. 2-Elf crossing arms, slight smirk, raised eyebrow, skeptical expression. 3-Elf raising hands to cheeks in surprised emotion. 4-Elf with angry facial expression screaming at person._\n\n##### Camera reveals\n\nSlowly pan across a scene to uncover details, focus attention, or add a cinematic layer to your concept presentation\n\n_Animation Prompt: Castle, perched on rocky cliffs, ancient stone walls, towering turrets, drone shot zoom out to show adventurer back standing on mountain looking at castle, camera focus shift to person, blurs out background, illustrative style_\n\n##### Apparel Try On\n\nAnimate a model trying on apparel, turning in frame, or walking through space to bring fashion and product visuals to life.\n\n_Sketch, render, remove background, try on, animate. Animate prompt: Guy turns around, puts on the hood of the jacket and walks away from the camera._\n\n#### Access & Availability\n\nSince Animate is still in beta, each plan includes a limited number of animation credits per month. guide\n\n# How your sketches guide AI\n\nYour sketch provides the foundation that Vizcom builds upon. guide\n\n# Prompts as design intent\n\n### Prompts serve as a bridge between your visual thinking and the AI's interpretation capabilities.\n\n##### Effective prompting\n\nA good prompt acts as a clear bridge between your visual thinking and the AIâ€™s interpretive capabilities. It provides structure without limiting creativity by:\n\n- Specifying details that are hard to express in a sketch (e.g., materials, lighting)\n\n- Highlighting areas open to exploration\n\n- Including relevant technical rendering parameters\n\n\nStrong prompts guide the AI by clarifying your intent while still allowing room for creative interpretation and variation.\n\nWhen a prompt is vague, inconsistent, or overly broad, the AI may misinterpret your design intent. This can lead to outcomes that:\n\n- Overlook important visual or material details\n\n- Default to bland or generic results\n\n- Drift significantly from your intended direction\n\n\nThis often occurs when the sketch is ambiguous and the prompt lacks sufficient guidance to steer the AI effectively.\n\n**Example:**\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/b19ZwALShA90IJxliTbq1zI4OMA.png)\n\n##### Vague prompting\n\nWhen a prompt is vague, inconsistent, or overly broad, the AI may misinterpret your design intent. Here's a detailed look at the key aspects that define the company:\n\n### **Security**\n\nVizcom's security measures are robust and proactive. Utilizing AWS for hosting, and integrating tools like Datadog and Sentry, the company actively monitors for potential threats and responds swiftly. Regular security audits and SOC 2 Type 1 certification further demonstrate Vizcom's dedication to creating a secure environment that guards against unauthorized access and potential breaches.\n\n### **Data Protection**\n\nData protection is a fundamental aspect of Vizcom's operations. The company's web-based tool for industrial designers employs multi-layered security controls, including encryption and access restrictions, to ensure that sensitive product designs from large enterprise clients are kept confidential. Automation with Pulumi streamlines security management, enhancing overall data integrity.\n\n### **Privacy**\n\nVizcom's privacy approach is client-centric, going beyond legal compliance. The SOC 2 Type 1 certification is evidence of strict privacy controls, ensuring that sensitive client information, such as personal details and business-related data, is handled with the utmost care. Regular privacy training for employees aligns the company with international privacy standards.\n\n### **Ownership**\n\nVizcom recognizes the importance of intellectual property rights, ensuring that clients maintain ownership of their designs and ideas. The platform's architecture supports a smooth transition from idea to concept, without compromising ownership. Clear agreements and transparent policies reflect Vizcom's respect for creators' rights.\n\n### **Responsible AI Development**\n\nVizcom's in-house AI development emphasizes responsible and ethical practices. The process includes transparency in algorithm design, fairness in application, and ongoing evaluation to ensure alignment with ethical standards. Collaboration with external experts and adherence to industry guidelines contribute to the responsible integration of AI into the platform.\n\n### **Risk Assessment and Mitigation**\n\nVizcom's comprehensive risk management includes:\n\n- **Abuse & Misuse:** Strict access controls and monitoring to prevent unauthorized use.\n\n- **Compliance:** A dedicated legal team ensures adherence to legal and regulatory requirements.\n\n- **Environmental Impact:** Sustainable practices to minimize ecological footprint.\n\n- **Transparency:** Open communication about AI model creation and governance.\n\n- **Fairness & Bias:** Regular assessments to ensure non-discriminatory AI practices.\n\n- **Performance:** Continuous monitoring and updates for maintaining optimal performance.\n\n- **Privacy:** A privacy-first approach, aligned with global privacy standards.\n\n\n### **Conclusion**\n\nVizcom's commitment to responsible AI, robust security, data protection, privacy, and ownership is not just a statement but a practice embedded in every aspect of the company's operations. The detailed approach ensures that clients can trust Vizcom with their most sensitive information and ideas.\n\nVizcom's leadership in these areas, backed by tangible actions and clear policies, makes it a reliable choice for industrial designers and large enterprises. His work, particularly with Vizcom, showcases a symbiotic relationship between human creativity and machine intelligence, transforming the way we think about design, collaboration, and innovation.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/vkXpNNtCgDM2ceR0t4KKRG110.jpg)\n\nAs we explore Mueller's philosophy and workflow, we see a journey that begins with a solitary idea and evolves through constant exchange into a fully fleshed-out product idea, ready to be refined and introduced to the world.\n\nBelow, Dennis shares his insights and experiences, offering a first-person perspective into how he's integrated AI tools like Vizcom into his creative processes.\n\n## What's a misconception about AI's role in design?\n\n_The Creative Co-Worker_\n\nPeople are always afraid of the New. IÂ´m always curious about it. So I started using AI design tools in 2021 and back then I thought it was kind of a nice gadget to play around with but did not see the whole potential behind it.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/cHa5zOuBtu6s0zSVZ8MKmOIAwU.jpg)\n\nFor sure AI in general is under discussion and that's an important thing to do now to compare the positive and negative effects it could cause. But to find out the potential, you need to try it and judge later on. I started using Vizcom heavily at the beginning of 2023. A thing I fell in love with was the intuitive user interface. Nothing distracts you, the functions are very clear and the settings are not overwhelming.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/sFvVJQZaZzxQcB3pOMwf79SRya0.jpg)\n\nI always begin with a hand-drawn sketch and a self-written prompt, laying the groundwork for my ideas in a traditional creative manner before digital rendering. Many misunderstand this part, but to me, it's akin to an early-stage collaborator where I share initial concepts shortly after starting a project. Effective communication, even in these nascent stages, is crucial for success. Engaging in clear, unbiased exchanges with tools like AI can significantly enhance the outcome.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/dGfMRfjqDVl6lYdPbWcE6E6GU.jpg)![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/SbOcnjWzlbhyvk1x7IcAHye2wug.jpg)\n\nIÂ´m not saying that you should always use AI tools but in some cases, it makes sense, especially when you're stuck with new ideas and have a kind of writer's block in design. Then I always use a sketch and put it into Vizcom to create new ideas or give the initial idea a twist, edge, and/or life.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/NoIjKc8OtUFvj9Pr55sy33nZUfQ.jpg)\n\nAnother misconception is that AI tools should just render out the idea you had in your mind. I use Vizcom very organically and go with the flow. But what does this mean? I never get stuck too much on that first idea.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/eLnvu7i3dCxxdSR9axmHJwZqKaE.jpg)\n\nI trust my instincts and stay alert for the intriguing. This approach requires a creative lens to spot and appreciate unique elements. Whenever something catches my eye, even a minor detail, I make a note of it to possibly blend with other designs, shapes, or materials later. I frequently employ Procreate for initial sketches, then transfer these ideas into Vizcom to add realism and depth.\n\nTry to see Vizcom as an extension of your creative mind rather than an enemy who's stealing your job. At the end, we still guide the whole journey and make the decisions.\n\n## How do you balance\xa0Vizcom\xa0with human-centric design?\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/XLNcJ33VfE5GkY9zgVmZr0qbhI.jpg)\n\nIn designing footwear, starting with the last is crucial, particularly for performance shoes, to ensure proper ergonomics and fit from the beginning. Typically, I begin with a side-view sketch as my foundation. From there, I refine my ideas by moving on to Vizcom. This stage helps me either polish my initial concept into a rendered version or explore new design directions.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/DmmDU4u7ivgmfG8edxDM4Uyc6s.jpg)![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/a5bVjEVmJNi1fE0jnX8pxv54s.png)\n\nA common misunderstanding about AI is thinking that once it generates hyper-realistic images, the work is complete. However, creating designs that truly cater to human needs involves multiple steps to ensure the final product is genuinely effective.\n\n## How do you see AI influencing the design process in the next 5 years?\n\nI told a lot of friends that it's an exciting time to be a designer. Sure we have some serious challenges\xa0to tackle but as soon as everybody understands the power of collaboration beautiful things can happen. Collaborations in all ways, people from different departments, companies, countries, and backgrounds, but also man and machines.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/dDRydkT3A86ByRhyeGHSscLyWk.jpg)\n\nIn the next 5 years, a lot of repetitive activities will be heavily influenced\xa0by AI in design. CMFs, Tech Packs, 3d to manufacture are just a few topics creatives won't spend as much time on as they used to. This is amazing because then we will have more resources to invest in storytelling, experimenting, questioning the status quo, finding real sustainable solutions, and interacting with people more often again.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/GMeBM4XciIEVHHKMfBtxUs81EVw.jpg)\n\nBesides the quantity and quality of creative ideas within a shorter timeframe\xa0will increase a lot. So, there needs to be good designers and core team members to judge all these results to take the right path.\n\n## Describe the most exciting aspect of merging industrial design with\xa0Vizcom.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/XiJCVF4WVtWiMXX5C5NwWW4ucks.jpg)![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/JphX3wEwQL95BYgy2tAAPlnlxkc.jpg)\n\nAs mentioned in the beginning, the real strength is having a coworker now all the time. Playing ping pong with ideas creates a unique energy\xa0where sometimes it doesn't\xa0feel like work. It's more like being in a flow state, comparable with a runner's high where one idea leads to the next.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/bnVkoQlTiuNuYdF9q2HfsYqqLI.jpg)\n\nIt can get you addicted in a way. It's that magical moment when Vizcom renders out a new vision in such a hyper-realistic way, that you feel that there is something special the world did not see before.\n\n## How can young designers & students best prepare for the AI-driven design landscape?\n\nI've always been a huge fan of building fundamentals\xa0in the beginning. Especially living in a digital world, we need to learn the basics like model making to understand our physical world first. This is a very important\xa0step a lot of creatives nowadays are missing.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/CNSdcLJxOafbAYIF1XwfzWNBVI.jpg)\n\nTo create innovative designs that stand the test of time, we must master ergonomics, refined silhouettes, seamless surface transitions, and the principles of the golden ratio, among other skills. Today, we are excited to continue this mission by enabling you to generate 3D geometry from a photo or drawing. This step forward makes 3D design more intuitive, enabling you to see your idea in a new dimension.\n\n3D models play an essential role of the design process, communicating scale, form, and materials that sketches often lack. They provide us with an understanding of how an object will feel rather than just how it looks. We're able to assess these models to make decisions, and determine how to move forward with a project.\n\nGiven the complexity of traditional CAD programs, creating 3D is not often part of the ideation process. Translating ideas from paper to 3D can be difficult, and takes a great deal of time to accurately capture the proportions and gesture of a sketch. This lengthy process discourages broad exploration, pushing designers towards early decision-making rather than expansive idea exploration.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/w9TpW9Hv61qvwL9w0Pol9E.png)\n\nIn Vizcom, your drawing acts as the foundation for generating a 3d model. Once your sketch is rendered, a 3D model can be created in a matter of seconds. By rapidly bridging dimensions, this feature offers immediate feedback on how an idea looks and feels from all angles.\n\n![](https://framerusercontent.com/images/HS0odR8zVvUkSR3IRdFzAp1ns.jpg)\n\n3D can be generated from more than just a sketch. Capturing a well-lit prototype allows Vizcom to reconstruct the geometry and digitize your work.\n\nGenerating a 3D model is not the end of the iteration process inside of Vizcom. Models can be viewed as layers inside Vizcom, allowing you to use it as an underlay to continue sketching and generating new ideas.\n\nWe believe these new tools will change the way we design and develop ideas. With the ability to generate 3D from drawings, we hope designers will find themselves liberated to experiment more freely, push the boundaries of creativity, and achieve a deeper understanding of their concepts earlier in the process. This is only our first step into the world of generative 3D. We continue developing new technologies and tools that empower designers to imagine their ideas no matter the dimension.\n\nIn the upcoming weeks, we will be rolling out this feature inside an updated drawing interface. You can list these keywords in order of importance to help shape the generated image. However, describing more complex designs can be challenging, as Vizcom doesn't interpret prompt context the way a human would. This means that assigning specific colors, materials, or features can sometimes be hit or miss. In such cases, using the selection tools can help you apply design elements more precisely.\n\nLetâ€™s take a look at an example.\n\nSuppose you want to design a modern sneaker with multiple patches.
